### Post by gordintoronto on 2016-06-18
I'm 99% certain that you are better off with one card than two, which will only interfere with each other.

---

### Post by uRock on 2016-06-18
How fast is your ISP connection? Load balancing through two connections won't be very beneficial, if they're connecting to one AP(access point) that has less bandwidth than just one of the NICs.

Are the two WiFi cards connecting to the same AP? If they are connecting to multiple APs, then this link may be helpful. [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UbuntuBonding](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UbuntuBonding)

---

### Post by him610 on 2016-06-18
You neglected to state your connection type. Is it FIOS, cable, or dial-up? Do you have a wireless router and wireless cards capable of supporting IEEE 802.11AC? 
Go to [www.speedtest.net/]("www.speedtest.net/") What is your download/upload speed?
To boost your internet speed -
Get FIOS, or pay your cable provider for highest speed available, don't use dial-up, upgrade all of your wireless devices to latest IEEE 802.11AC technology, or use wired Cat6 connections.;)

---

### Post by potar30 on 2016-06-18
I am using just one card but i have a problem with the speed , i have two routers with 4.0mb download and 0.2 upload each , what i want it is to make my network speed 8 mb with using 2 wireless cards

i have two routers with 4.0mb download and 0.2 upload each , what i want it is to make my network speed 8 mb with using 2 wireless cards , is it possible to connect to two different wifis with tow exterior wireless cards ? i am running ubuntu and they are working but the connection are not , only one works i need them to work both , thanks

i sont have any of that , i have two routers ( 4mb up , 0.2mb each ) without any Ethernet cables  , which mean two different wireless networks , i need them both to work with my computer

---

### Post by DuckHook on 2016-06-18
Welcome to the forums, potar30.

It is important to read what uRock has posted.

Network throughput doesn't work the way you may be thinking. If you have two routers connected to the same AP, then you will merely be dividing your throughput in half for each router if they are used simultaneously. However, if they each connect to separate APs, then you can realize some speed increases by following the link that uRock has provided. Two routers running separate wireless networks is immaterial. The key is whether they connect to two different Access Points.

---
